GROQ_API_KEYS:\n            try:\n                self.groq_clients.append(Groq(api_key=key))\n            except Exception as e:\n                print(f"Failed to initialize Groq client: {e}")\n        \n        self.groq_index = 0\n        self.groq_lock = Lock()\n        \n        # Aristotle client (using Groq with deterministic settings)\n        try:\n            self.aristotle_client = self.aristotle_available = False\n        \n        # Onboard LLM (simulated fallback)\n        self.onboard_available = True\n    \n    def get_groq_client(self):\n        """Get next Groq client with round-robin"""\n        with self.groq_lock:\n            if not self.groq_clients:\n                return None\n            client = self.groq_clients[self.groq_index]\n            self.groq_index = (self.groq_index + 1) % len(self.groq_clients)\n            return client\n    \n    def call_groq(self, messages, temperature=0.7):\n        """Call Groq API"""\n        client = self.get_groq_client()\n        if not client:\n            raise Exception("No Groq clients available")\n        \n        response = client.chat.completions.create(\n            model="llama-3.3-70b-versatile",\n            messages=messages,\n            temperature=temperature,\n            max_tokens=1024\n        )\n        return response.choices[0].message.content\n    \n    def call_aristotle(self, messages):\n        """Call Aristotle API (deterministic)"""\n        if not self.aristotle_available:\n            raise Exception("Aristotle client not available")\n        \n        response = self.aristotle_client.chat.completions.create(\n            model="llama-3.3-70b-versatile",\n            messages=messages,\n            temperature=0.1,  # Deterministic\n            max_tokens=1024\n        )\n        return response.choices[0].message.content\n    \n    def call_onboard(self, messages):\n        """Call onboard LLM (fallback)"""\n        # Simulated response for now\n        return "Onboard LLM response (fallback mode)"\n\n# Initialize LLM router\nllm_router = LLMRouter()\n\n# ===== MURPHY SYSTEM STATE =====\nsystem_state = {\n ]\n    for comp in components:\n        system_state[\'components\'][comp[\'id\']] = comp\n    return components\n\ndef create_state(state_type, label, parent_id=None, state_id=None):\n    if state_id file_path=\\\\"MURPHY_SYSTEM_ANALYSIS.md\\\\">\\\\\\\\n# Murphy System - Critical Issues Analysis\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n## Section 1: Understanding Confirmation\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\nThe Murphy system is a transparent, agentic business operating system that provides real-time visibility into autonomous agent operations through a terminal-driven interface with interactive visualizations. The system uses living documents, swarm-based task execution, and domain-specific validation gates to automate business operations while maintaining human-in-the-loop oversight. Users can observe system behavior, interact with components to understand operations, and control the automation workflow through a unified interface.\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n## Section 2: Component Definitions\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Agents\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Autonomous entities that execute specific tasks within assigned domains (e.g., Sales Agent, Engineering Agent, Financial Agent)\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: Animated nodes with status indicators (active/idle/error), task progress bars, and connection lines to related components\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: Click to view current task, logs, configuration, and manually override or redirect\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: Sales Agent processing a lead and updating CRM\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Components\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Modular building blocks of the system (LLM Router, Domain Engine, Gate Builder, Swarm Generator)\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: Static panels with active indicators showing operational status\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: Click to view parameters, health status, and recent activity logs\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: LLM Router showing which API (Groq/Aristotle/Onboard) is being used for a request\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Gates\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Validation checkpoints that ensure outputs meet standards (regulatory, security, business rules)\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: Gateway symbols that light up green/red based on pass/fail\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: Click to view validation criteria, test results, and override permissions\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: Regulatory gate checking if generated content complies with GDPR\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Systems\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Complete operational workflows (e.g., Contract Generation System, Product Development System)\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: Flowchart diagrams showing process stages and decision points\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: Click to pause/resume, modify parameters, or inject manual steps\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: Complete lead-to-close sales system\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### States\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Snapshot conditions of system components at a point in time\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: State tree in sidebar with parent-child relationships\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: Click to view state details, regenerate from this state, or rollback\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: Document state showing \\\\"MAGNIFIED\\\\" with domain expertise depth of 60%\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Deterministic Systems\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Processes with predictable, repeatable outcomes (Aristotle API, temp 0.1)\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: Blue-colored components with lock icons indicating stable behavior\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: View deterministic rules, input/output mappings, and validation logs\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: Code compliance verification using Aristotle\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Verified Systems\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Systems that have passed all validation gates and are approved for production\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: Gold badges or checkmarks indicating certified status\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: View certification history, gate results, and approval chain\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: A contract generation system that passed legal and compliance gates\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Generated Systems\\\\\\\\n- **Definition**: Systems created dynamically by the Murphy runtime based on requirements\\\\\\\\n- **Visual Representation**: Dashed outlines showing they\\\\\\\\\\\'re AI-generated with generation metadata\\\\\\\\n- **User Interaction**: Review generation process, modify generated code/logic, or regenerate\\\\\\\\n- **Example Use Case**: Custom workflow system generated for a specific business need\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n## Section 3: Issue Diagnosis\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Issue 1: Non-functional Complete UI\\\\\\\\n**Root Cause Analysis:**\\\\\\\\nThe `murphy_complete_ui.html` file loads successfully and the JavaScript is initialized (window.addEventListener(\\\\\\\\\\\'load\\\\\\\\\\\')), but the interface lacks:\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n1. **Real-time visualization components** - No canvas, SVG, or graph elements for showing agent operations\\\\\\\\n2. **Interactive state tree** - No clickable state nodes with parent-child relationships\\\\\\\\n3. **Live agent activity display** - No animated nodes showing which agents are active\\\\\\\\n4. **Process flow visualization** - No flowchart or diagram showing system workflows\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Technical Diagnosis:**\\\\\\\\n- File: `/workspace/murphy_test_extract/murphy_complete_ui.html` (1319 lines)\\\\\\\\n- Backend API: Working correctly (tested `/api/status` and `/api/initialize`)\\\\\\\\n- Frontend JavaScript: Basic tab switching and API calls exist\\\\\\\\n- Missing: Visualization library integration, real-time Plan Review Interface\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Purpose:** A dedicated UI component for reviewing, modifying, and managing AI-generated plans before execution.\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Interactive Controls - Detailed Behavior:**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Accept Button:**\\\\\\\\n- Validates plan completeness and feasibility\\\\\\\\n- Triggers execution workflow initiation\\\\\\\\n- Creates execution record with timestamp and user ID\\\\\\\\n- Transitions plan state from \\\\"under_review\\\\" to \\\\"approved\\\\"\\\\\\\\n- Notifies relevant stakeholders\\\\\\\\n- Archives plan in execution history\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Edit Button:**\\\\\\\\n- Opens plan in edit mode with inline modification capabilities\\\\\\\\n- Tracks changes with version control\\\\\\\\n- Allows modification of: steps, parameters, assignments, timelines\\\\\\\\n- Validates edits against system constraints\\\\\\\\n- Requires re-approval after substantial changes\\\\\\\\n- Preserves original plan as previous version\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Reject Button:**\\\\\\\\n- Dismisses plan without execution\\\\\\\\n- Prompts for rejection reason (required field)\\\\\\\\n- Logs rejection with feedback for learning\\\\\\\\n- Optionally triggers plan regeneration with feedback incorporated\\\\\\\\n- Transitions plan state to \\\\"rejected\\\\"\\\\\\\\n- Notifies plan creator/system\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Magnify Button:**\\\\\\\\n- Triggers deeper analysis of plan components\\\\\\\\n- Expands high-level steps into detailed sub-steps\\\\\\\\n- Adds resource requirements, time estimates, dependencies\\\\\\\\n- Incorporates risk analysis and contingencies\\\\\\\\n- May invoke specialized domain modules for detailed planning\\\\\\\\n- Creates new plan version with expanded detail\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Simplify Button:**\\\\\\\\n- Consolidates redundant or overly detailed steps\\\\\\\\n- Removes unnecessary complexity while preserving intent\\\\\\\\n- Merges related actions into higher-level tasks\\\\\\\\n- Optimizes for execution efficiency\\\\\\\\n- Validates that simplified plan still achieves objectives\\\\\\\\n- Creates new plan version with reduced complexity\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Solidify Button:**\\\\\\\\n- Converts plan to concrete, executable specifications\\\\\\\\n- Generates specific parameter values (no placeholders)\\\\\\\\n- Assigns resources and responsibilities\\\\\\\\n- Creates detailed execution timeline\\\\\\\\n- Generates validation checkpoints and success criteria\\\\\\\\n- Prepares plan for bot/automation deployment\\\\\\\\n- Transitions plan state to \\\\"executable\\\\"\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Specification Requirements:**\\\\\\\\n- Define the plan data structure at each state: draft, under_review, magnified, simplified, solidified, approved, rejected, executed\\\\\\\\n- Document state transition diagram with all possible paths\\\\\\\\n- Specify plan versioning scheme (e.g., semantic versioning)\\\\\\\\n- Detail the feedback capture mechanism and data model\\\\\\\\n- Explain how user modifications are validated against system constraints\\\\\\\\n- Define access control (who can review/approve different plan types)\\\\\\\\n- Specify UI/UX requirements (layout, responsiveness, accessibility)\\\\\\\\n- Document integration with execution engine\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n---\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### 4. Terminal/Orchestrator\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Purpose:** The central command interpreter and routing system that processes all user inputs and coordinates system components.\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Key Capabilities:**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Natural Language Processing:**\\\\\\\\n- Intent classification\\\\\\\\n- Entity extraction\\\\\\\\n- Context resolution\\\\\\\\n- Ambiguity detection\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Command Interpretation:**\\\\\\\\n- Parse structured commands\\\\\\\\n- Validate syntax and parameters\\\\\\\\n- Resolve command aliases\\\\\\\\n- Handle command chaining\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Confidence Scoring:**\\\\\\\\n- Calculate interpretation confidence (0-100%)\\\\\\\\n- Define confidence thresholds:\\\\\\\\n  - High (>85%): Auto-execute\\\\\\\\n  - Medium (60-85%): Confirm with user\\\\\\\\n  - Low (<60%): Request clarification\\\\\\\\n- Document scoring algorithm factors\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Human-in-the-Loop Checkpoints:**\\\\\\\\n- Trigger when confidence below threshold\\\\\\\\n- Present interpretation to user for confirmation\\\\\\\\n- Offer alternative interpretations\\\\\\\\n- Learn from user corrections\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Command Routing:**\\\\\\\\n- Decision tree for routing to appropriate modules\\\\\\\\n- Load balancing for distributed components\\\\\\\\n- Priority queue management\\\\\\\\n- Fallback routing strategies\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Workflow Management:**\\\\\\\\n- Initiate system setup workflows\\\\\\\\n- Coordinate multi-step operations\\\\\\\\n- Manage workflow state\\\\\\\\n- Convert validated workflows to presets\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Specification Requirements:**\\\\\\\\n- Document the complete routing decision tree (use flowchart or pseudocode)\\\\\\\\n- Define error handling strategies for each component type\\\\\\\\n- Specify logging requirements (what, when, format, retention)\\\\\\\\n- Detail audit trail requirements for compliance\\\\\\\\n- Explain context management across multi-turn interactions (session state, conversation history)\\\\\\\\n- Define escalation procedures for unhandled scenarios\\\\\\\\n- Specify performance requirements (response time, throughput)\\\\\\\\n- Document API interfaces for component integration\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n---\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### 5. Preset System\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Purpose:** A mechanism for capturing, storing, and reusing validated workflows as executable presets, building a comprehensive automation library over time.\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Preset Generation:**\\\\\\\\nPresets are generated based on:\\\\\\\\n- Domain-specific best practices and industry standards\\\\\\\\n- Validated generative workflows that have proven successful\\\\\\\\n- Cross-domain adaptation when workflow patterns are comparable\\\\\\\\n- Control theory specifications created through reasoning\\\\\\\\n- Template modules that meet current system standards\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Preset Structure:**\\\\\\\\nEach preset must encapsulate:\\\\\\\\n- **Metadata**: Name, description, category, tags, version, author, creation date\\\\\\\\n- **Trigger Conditions**: Events or criteria that activate the preset\\\\\\\\n- **Execution Steps**: Ordered sequence of actions with parameters\\\\\\\\n- **Required Permissions**: Roles/access levels needed to execute\\\\\\\\n- **Expected Outcomes**: Success criteria and validation checks\\\\\\\\n- **Dependencies**: Required system components or external resources\\\\\\\\n- **Configuration Options**: Customizable parameters for different contexts\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Preset Lifecycle:**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n1. **Creation:**\\\\\\\\n   - Generated from domain knowledge\\\\\\\\n   - Converted from successful generative workflows\\\\\\\\n   - Manually authored by domain experts\\\\\\\\n   - Adapted from existing presets\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n2. **Validation:**\\\\\\\\n   - Quality gate checks (completeness, correctness, safety)\\\\\\\\n   - Test execution in sandbox environment\\\\\\\\n   - Peer review process\\\\\\\\n   - Compliance verification\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n3. **Storage:**\\\\\\\\n   - Centralized preset repository\\\\\\\\n   - Version control integration\\\\\\\\n   - Metadata indexing for search\\\\\\\\n   - Access control enforcement\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n4. **Retrieval:**\\\\\\\\n   - Search by keyword, category, tag\\\\\\\\n   - Recommendation based on context\\\\\\\\n   - Similarity matching to user needs\\\\\\\\n   - Popularity and success rate ranking\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n5. **Execution:**\\\\\\\\n   - Parameter binding and validation\\\\\\\\n   - Permission verification\\\\\\\\n   - Execution monitoring\\\\\\\\n   - Result logging and feedback collection\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n6. **Versioning:**\\\\\\\\n   - Semantic versioning (major.minor.patch)\\\\\\\\n   - Change tracking and documentation\\\\\\\\n   - Backward compatibility management\\\\\\\\n   - Deprecation notices\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n7. **Deprecation:**\\\\\\\\n   - Criteria for obsolescence\\\\\\\\n   - Migration path to replacement presets\\\\\\\\n   - Archive process\\\\\\\\n   - Historical access for audit purposes\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Template System for Code Generation:**\\\\\\\\n- Define template structure and syntax\\\\\\\\n- Specify variable substitution mechanism\\\\\\\\n- Document template validation process\\\\\\\\n- Explain how templates ensure code quality and standards compliance\\\\\\\\n- Provide examples of templates for common patterns\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Quality Gates and Promotion Criteria:**\\\\\\\\n- Define quality metrics (test coverage, error rate, performance)\\\\\\\\n- Specify promotion levels (draft, beta, production, deprecated)\\\\\\\\n- Document approval workflow for promotion\\\\\\\\n- Establish monitoring and feedback mechanisms\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Specification Requirements:**\\\\\\\\n- Complete preset data schema (JSON or YAML format)\\\\\\\\n- Categorization taxonomy (hierarchical structure)\\\\\\\\n- Tagging system and conventions\\\\\\\\n- Search and filtering capabilities\\\\\\\\n- Cross-domain adaptation rules and constraints\\\\\\\\n- Integration with version control systems\\\\\\\\n- Preset analytics and usage tracking\\\\\\\\n- Import/export functionality for preset sharing\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n---\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### 6. Domain Coverage\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**IMPORTANT CLARIFICATION:** \\\\\\\\nThe following are CATEGORIES, not domains. Actual domains are specific business contexts (e.g., \\\\"engineering firm that doesn\\\\\\\\\\\'t own its building, witnesses manufacturing equipment testing they designed, but doesn\\\\\\\\\\\'t manufacture\\\\").\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Specification Approach:**\\\\\\\\n1. Define the category structure and capabilities below\\\\\\\\n2. Provide 2-3 complete example domain implementations showing how different business contexts would configure and use these categories\\\\\\\\n3. Demonstrate the system\\\\\\\\\\\'s flexibility and adaptability\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Category Types:**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**A. Physical Systems** (interact with sensors and operate physical aspects)\\\\\\\\n- Building Automation\\\\\\\\n- Manufacturing\\\\\\\\n- Energy Management\\\\\\\\n- SCADA (Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition)\\\\\\\\n- Finance (physical asset tracking, inventory)\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**B. Agentic Systems** (AI-driven decision support and automation)\\\\\\\\n- Executive Branch (reactive business piloting, constraint management, metrics tracking, plan adherence monitoring)\\\\\\\\n- Marketing\\\\\\\\n- Proposals and Sales\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**C. Hybrid Systems** (agentic approval actions based on rules and learning, with physical execution)\\\\\\\\n- Turnovers\\\\\\\\n- Operations\\\\\\\\n- Drafting\\\\\\\\n- Manpower Planning\\\\\\\\n- Procurement\\\\\\\\n- Project Management\\\\\\\\n- Delivery and Logistics\\\\\\\\n- Revision Control\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**D. Shadow System** (personal AI assistant)\\\\\\\\nAn agent that learns position-specific reasoning and attempts to automate tasks for individuals. Key characteristics:\\\\\\\\n- Belongs to the person doing the work\\\\\\\\n- Can be licensed to non-competing companies\\\\\\\\n- Learns from user behavior and preferences\\\\\\\\n- Provides personalized automation recommendations\\\\\\\\n- (Include additional features identified in the analysis)\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**For Each Category, Document:**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n1. **Primary Use Cases:**\\\\\\\\n   - Top 5-10 scenarios where this category is used\\\\\\\\n   - Typical workflows and processes\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n2. **Key Commands:**\\\\\\\\n   - Command list with syntax and parameters\\\\\\\\n   - Usage examples\\\\\\\\n   - Integration with other categories\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n3. **Integration Points:**\\\\\\\\n   - Data flows to/from other categories\\\\\\\\n   - Shared resources and dependencies\\\\\\\\n   - Event triggers and notifications\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n4. **Data Models:**\\\\\\\\n   - Core entities and attributes\\\\\\\\n   - Relationships between entities\\\\\\\\n   - Data validation rules\\\\\\\\n   - Storage requirements\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n5. **Metrics and KPIs:**\\\\\\\\n   - Performance indicators tracked\\\\\\\\n   - Reporting capabilities\\\\\\\\n   - Dashboard visualizations\\\\\\\\n   - Alert thresholds\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n6. **Configuration Options:**\\\\\\\\n   - Parameters that vary by domain context\\\\\\\\n   - Customization capabilities\\\\\\\\n   - Default settings and best practices\\\\\\\\n   - Configuration validation\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Example Domain Implementations Required (2-3 complete examples):**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\nFor each example domain, show:\\\\\\\\n- Business context description\\\\\\\\n- Category configuration choices\\\\\\\\n- Customized workflows\\\\\\\\n- Integration patterns\\\\\\\\n- Sample commands and outputs\\\\\\\\n- Metrics dashboard\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\nSuggested example domains:\\\\\\\\n1. Engineering consulting firm (design focus, no manufacturing, leased facilities)\\\\\\\\n2. Manufacturing company (owns facilities, produces goods, manages supply chain)\\\\\\\\n3. Service-based business (minimal physical infrastructure, heavy agentic focus)\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n---\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### 7. System Setup & Constraint Management\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Purpose:** The initialization process that configures the Murphy System for a specific domain context, establishing operational parameters, constraints, and best practices.\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Swarm-Based Setup Process:**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\nThe setup employs a distributed, collaborative approach where each category agent:\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n1. **Generates Best Practices:**\\\\\\\\n   - Analyzes domain context\\\\\\\\n   - Retrieves industry-specific best practices from knowledge base\\\\\\\\n   - Proposes category-specific operational guidelines\\\\\\\\n   - Identifies optimization opportunities\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n2. **Incorporates Regulatory Knowledge:**\\\\\\\\n   - Identifies applicable regulations (OSHA, EPA, SOX, GDPR, etc.)\\\\\\\\n   - Uses regulations as reference for generating validation gates\\\\\\\\n   - Creates compliance checkpoints\\\\\\\\n   - Documents regulatory requirements\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n3. **Builds System Specification:**\\\\\\\\n   - Defines category configuration\\\\\\\\n   - Specifies integration points with other categories\\\\\\\\n   - Establishes data models and workflows\\\\\\\\n   - Creates constraint rules\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n4. **Generates Implementation Code:**\\\\\\\\n   - Uses template modules to generate code\\\\\\\\n   - Ensures compliance with system standards\\\\\\\\n   - Implements validation gates\\\\\\\\n   - Creates test cases\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n5. **Self-Analysis and Error Correction:**\\\\\\\\n   - Executes generated code in sandbox\\\\\\\\n   - Identifies errors and issues\\\\\\\\n   - Uses magnify/solidify/codify analysis to fix problems\\\\\\\\n   - Iterates until validation passes\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n6. **Cross-Category Validation:**\\\\\\\\n   - Queries Librarian with questions like: \\\\"Will this work with the current infrastructure?\\\\"\\\\\\\\n   - Checks for conflicts with other category configurations\\\\\\\\n   - Validates integration points\\\\\\\\n   - Ensures system-wide consistency\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Constraint Management:**\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Constraint Types:**\\\\\\\\n- **Hard Constraints:** Cannot be violated (regulatory, safety, physical limits)\\\\\\\\n- **Soft Constraints:** Preferences that can be overridden with justification\\\\\\\\n- **Dynamic Constraints:** Change based on context or conditions\\\\\\\\n- **Learned Constraints:** Derived from operational data and patterns\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Constraint Lifecycle:**\\\\\\\\n- Discovery and definition\\\\\\\\n- Validation and testing\\\\\\\\n- Activation and enforcement\\\\\\\\n- Monitoring and adjustment\\\\\\\\n- Deprecation and removal\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n**Specification Requirements:**\\\\\\\\n- Document the setup workflow step-by-step\\\\\\\\n- Define the swarm coordination mechanism (how agents communicate and collaborate)\\\\\\\\n- Specify the knowledge base structure for best practices and regulations\\\\\\\\n- Detail the validation gate generation process\\\\\\\\n- Explain the error correction loop (magnify/solidify/codify)\\\\\\\\n- Define the Librarian query interface for setup agents\\\\\\\\n- Document constraint definition language or format\\\\\\\\n- Specify constraint enforcement mechanisms\\\\\\\\n- Detail the setup completion criteria and validation\\\\\\\\n- Explain how setup can be modified post-deployment\\\\\\\\n- Include rollback and recovery procedures\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n---\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n## ADDITIONAL SPECIFICATION REQUIREMENTS:\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n### Cross-Cutting Concerns:\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n1. **Security:**\\\\\\\\n   - **Simplify**: Consolidate redundant steps, remove complexity\n  - **Solidify**: Convert to executable specifications\n\n#### 4. **Full UI (murphy_complete_v2.html)**\n**Purpose**: Visual monitoring and interaction\n\n**What You See**:\n- **State Tree**: Hierarchical view of all system states (parent-child relationships)\n- **Agent Graph**: Visual representation of active agents and their connections\n- **Process Flow**: Flowchart showing workflows executing\n- **Sidebar Metrics**: Real-time system status\n- **Terminal**: Command input and output display\n\n**What You Can Do**:\n- Click states to view details\n- Click agents to see current tasks\n- Evolve states (create child states)\n- Regenerate states (re-generate with new parameters)\n- Rollback states (revert to parent)\n- Watch real-time updates via WebSocket\n\n---\n\n## Phase 3: Swarm Execution\n\n### How Swarms Work:\n\n#### **Swarm Types**:\n\n1. **Creative Swarm** (exploratory, diverse solutions)\n   -
